  <span id="freeText15461354233280481595" style="display:none">This book was a delight to read. I enjoyed every single page. I loved it! <br /><br />“There's always a bit of truth in each rumour, the trouble is finding out which bit.”<br /><br />This book is the sequel to The Magician’s Guild. It followed the continuation of Sonea’s story. In this novel she has entered the university to study magic but is met with resistance from some of her class members and teachers. But is she safe now? The High Lord Akkarin harbours a secret that is far darker than his black robes.<br /><br />I am in love with Sonea, she is such a strong empowering young woman. To be perfectly honest all the characters were really great, they were full bodied with great personalities, even if some of those personalities are pretty evil. <br /><br />The writing was simple yet descriptive. What I mean is even though the writing was not a challenge a fantastic picture of Sonea’s world was produced. Don’t get me wrong this wasn’t groundbreaking work of description but it gave a good overview of what characters are thinking and what their landscape is. <br /><br />I am so happy that I was reading a book with such a tiny, miniscule, amount of romance. Like, seriously, there was next to none. The plot was not fast, there wasn’t really too much going on in this novel. The main focus was on the relationship between Sonea and her tormentors and Sonea and The High Lord. There was little action as well throughout the novel, but right at the end there is a climax, and it was SO MUCH FUN!!! Even though the action and plot was slow there was still a lot going on with Sonea’s lessons and her exams and her growing relationships with certain characters, so it was far from a dull read.<br /> <br />I really liked this book. It has rekindled my love for adult fantasy. I do wish there was a little more going on throughout the novel but overall it was great fun! <br /><br />“What was natural and right? Who really knew? The world was never so simple that one person could have all the answers.”<br /><br />I recommend this book to fantasy and YA book lovers (even though this book is not YA it is quite similar to YA novels). <br /><br />5 stars.<br /><br />Happy reading! <br /><br />Love <br /><br />Hannah xoxo<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614678729" />
    <a title="Arminion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10664177-arminion"><img alt="Arminion" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341340920p2/10664177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614678729?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arminion" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arminion" href="/user/show/10664177-arminion">Arminion</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060575298" href="/book/show/806040.The_Novice">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614678729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6244126209764585426">At first I liked this book. Things were...moving forward. Very soon, however I became bored and frustrated. Why? Because of the whole bully business that goes for the ENTIRE book. It never stops. It just goes on and on and on. I really didn't know what I hated more, the fact that Sonea was acting like a punching bag that entire time, or the fact that Canavan devoted so much time to this trivial subplot. By the time Sonea finally shows some teeth, it's already too late and the feeling of victory </span>
  <span id="freeText6244126209764585426" style="display:none">At first I liked this book. Things were...moving forward. Very soon, however I became bored and frustrated. Why? Because of the whole bully business that goes for the ENTIRE book. It never stops. It just goes on and on and on. I really didn't know what I hated more, the fact that Sonea was acting like a punching bag that entire time, or the fact that Canavan devoted so much time to this trivial subplot. By the time Sonea finally shows some teeth, it's already too late and the feeling of victory is hollow and empty when we remember all the things she went through. And on top of that, Regin isn't a good villain. He is a caricature. I almost stopped reading when Sonea moves to the next class just to escape him and he does the SAME! Who DOES that?!<br />That reminded me of the bad Hollywood cliche: when our hero punches the villain, cuts him with a sword, shoots him in the face and runs him over with the car and the villain STILL stands up and continues to fight. I just said: come on! Enough of this whole Regin business! If I was in Sonea's shoes, that kid would already be in a river with a stone around his neck and to the hell with the Guild and High Lord!<br />I understood that Sonea is hopeless and kinda useless in the first book. She is basically a scared child. But here, she is a little bit more mature and more powerful and yet, she never stand up for herself but she keeps running away and hoping they will leave her alone. She still continues to use that tactic, regardless of the fact that it didn't work the first 38 times. Ugh.<br />Dannyl also gets a lot of attention. His story was a little bit more interesting than Sonea's but in the end it falls flat as it goes nowhere. The whole gay thing didn't really surprise me either.<br />All in all, it's a book that made me angry which in my book (pun intended) it's not a good thing. It's definitely a book that I won't be reading again.<br />I will however, continue with the trilogy just to see how this all wraps up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6244126209764585426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_948802931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/948802931" />
    <a title="Ornella (Nyx)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6282007-ornella-nyx"><img alt="Ornella (Nyx)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363660589p2/6282007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/948802931?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ornella (Nyx)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ornella (Nyx)" href="/user/show/6282007-ornella-nyx">Ornella (Nyx)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6282007-ornella-nyx?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948802931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10276810273856538176">There is something missing for me with these books. They are 'good' but not as engaging as I would like them to be, or more accurately I think they should have elicited more enthusiasm from me what with all that's going on. There is/was a serial killer on the loose, more problems for Sonea took place, Lorlen, Dannyl and Rothen encountered their own issues, and yet, it was kinds of blah. <br/><br/>I think it's the same problem as the last book. The pacing. Everything is just moving SO SLOWLY. The thing is </span>
  <span id="freeText10276810273856538176" style="display:none">There is something missing for me with these books. They are 'good' but not as engaging as I would like them to be, or more accurately I think they should have elicited more enthusiasm from me what with all that's going on. There is/was a serial killer on the loose, more problems for Sonea took place, Lorlen, Dannyl and Rothen encountered their own issues, and yet, it was kinds of blah. <br /><br />I think it's the same problem as the last book. The pacing. Everything is just moving SO SLOWLY. The thing is I usually don't mind the slow pacing as long as it can keep my interest, but these books are cutting it close. Whenever I stopped reading I would keep putting off getting back to the book, but it just wasn't that interesting. Yes there were problems but I never felt that sense of urgency or danger. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't know if this might be because I simply have never thought the High Lord to be the evil villain everyone keeps thinking he is, so I just don't see the danger. Sure their situation sucks but, that's it. Nothing more to it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The last two chapters were the only ones that eliciyed any kind of emotion from me (excitement) cause we are FINALLY getting somewhere. After, what like 800 pages between both books, we are actually getting to the meet of the problem. I just think it was 400 pages too long at this point. <br /><br />With that said I'll finish the trilogy because I it's a nice enough fantasy and I'd like to know Akkarin's secrets :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10276810273856538176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oscnZmYK/YniXuBRVqjuJAVjeIREqW6wJWUg7+0w4QBVvFjHJs4dK2Ms7cxar2loZqxQA/vtdG7tdJEcUiQffA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jRgiIdySM9gzn1H+14D3QJjymycIa8zlgKKRXMbvQVJ6Y12AnFbTerLtXGPbh3AM+z2zoLcv1jtIsyCvefu/Lg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18229079249601219721">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br/><br/>In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br/><br/>In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. T</span>
  <span id="freeText18229079249601219721" style="display:none">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br /><br />In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br /><br />In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. The second book of the trilogy, The Novice, was published in June 2002 and was nominated for the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Novel. The third book The High Lord was released in January 2003 and was nominated for the Best Novel Ditmar category. All three books entered Australian top ten SF bestseller lists.<br /><br />The Black Magician Trilogy reached the international market in 2004, published by HarperCollins’ EOS imprint in North America and Orbit Books in the UK. The trilogy is now rated by Nielsen BookScan as the most successful debut fantasy series of the last 10 years.<br /><br />Trudi’s second trilogy, Age of the Five, has also enjoyed bestselling success. Priestess of the White reached No.3 in the Sunday Times hardback fiction bestseller list, staying in the top ten for six weeks.<br /><br />In early 2006 Trudi signed a seven-figure contract with Orbit to write the prequel and sequel to the Black Magician Trilogy. The prequel, The Magician’s Apprentice was released in 2009 and won the Best Fantasy Novel category of the Aurealis Awards. She is now working on the sequel trilogy, and planning her next fantasy series, which will be set in an entirely new world.</span>
